//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/PR_secondary_119.svg/62px-PR_secondary_119.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_64" title="Puerto Rico Highway 64"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Ellipse_sign_64.svg/25px-Ellipse_sign_64.svg.png" decoding="async" width="25" height="25" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Ellipse_sign_64.svg/38px-Ellipse_sign_64.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Ellipse_sign_64.svg/50px-Ellipse_sign_64.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="192" data-file-height="192" /></a></span> <span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_104" title="Puerto Rico Highway 104"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Ellipse_sign_104.svg/31px-Ellipse_sign_104.svg.png" decoding="async" width="31" height="25" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Ellipse_sign_104.svg/47px-Ellipse_sign_104.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Ellipse_sign_104.svg/62px-Ellipse_sign_104.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="600" /></a></span></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/Geographic_Names_Information_System" title="Geographic Names Information System">GNIS</a> feature ID</th><td class="infobox-data">1611495<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.mayaguezpr.gov">www<wbr />.mayaguezpr<wbr />.gov</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Mayag\xc3\xbcez</b> (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">Spanish pronunciation:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;ma\xca\x9da\xcb\x88\xc9\xa3wes&#93;</a></span>, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1177148991"><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">locally</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;ma\xca\x9da\xcb\x88we\xca\x94&#93;</a></span>) is the ninth-largest<sup id="cite_ref-:0_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">municipality</a> in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>. It was founded as <b>Pueblo de Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora de la Candelaria de Mayag\xc3\xbcez</b> (Township of <a href="/wiki/Virgin_of_Candelaria" title="Virgin of Candelaria">Our Lady of Candelaria</a>), and is also known as <i>La Sultana del Oeste</i> (The Sultaness of the West), <i>Ciudad de las Aguas Puras</i> (City of Pure Waters), or <i>Ciudad del Mang\xc3\xb3</i> (Mango City). On April 6, 1894, the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Spain" title="Monarchy of Spain">Spanish Crown</a> granted it the formal title of <i>Excelente Ciudad de Mayag\xc3\xbcez</i> (Excellent City of Mayag\xc3\xbcez).<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Mayag\xc3\xbcez is located in the center of the western coast on the island of Puerto Rico. It has a population of 73,077, and it is the principal city of the <a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez_metropolitan_area" title="Mayag\xc3\xbcez metropolitan area">Mayag\xc3\xbcez Metropolitan Statistical Area</a> (pop. 213,831) and the <a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez_metropolitan_area#Combined_Statistical_Area" title="Mayag\xc3\xbcez metropolitan area">Mayag\xc3\xbcez\xe2\x80\x93Aguadilla, PR Combined Statistical Area</a> (pop. 467,599).<sup id="cite_ref-:0_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Mayag%C3%BCez" title="History of Mayag\xc3\xbcez">History of Mayag\xc3\xbcez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico" title="Timeline of Mayag\xc3\xbcez, Puerto Rico">Timeline of Mayag\xc3\xbcez, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez_metropolitan_area" title="Mayag\xc3\xbcez metropolitan area">Mayag\xc3\xbcez Metro Area</a> (and part of <a href="/wiki/A%C3%B1asco" class="mw-redirect" title="A\xc3\xb1asco">A\xc3\xb1asco</a>) lies today on two former <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Ta\xc3\xadno">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> <a href="/wiki/Chiefdom" title="Chiefdom">Cacicazgos (chiefdoms)</a>: Yaguex and Yag\xc3\xbceca, a region noted for its record of colonial resistance (i.e., <a href="/wiki/Urayo%C3%A1n" title="Urayo\xc3\xa1n">Urayo\xc3\xa1n</a> and <a href="/wiki/Legend_of_Diego_Salcedo" title="Legend of Diego Salcedo">Legend of Diego Salcedo</a>). The Tainos constituted the majority of the island\'s inhabitants at the time of contact with Europeans in 1493 and called it <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico#Etymology" title="Puerto Rico">Borik\xc3\xa9n or Borinquen</a>. Today, this appellation and its variations continue to designate the Island of Puerto Rico and its people. The Ta\xc3\xadnos came from South American branches of <a href="/wiki/Arawakan_languages" title="Arawakan languages">Arawakan speakers</a>, more specifically from modern-day <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, and lived in small villages, organized their society in clans and named their chiefs <a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">Cacique</a>. They were farmers who domesticated crops as <a href="/wiki/Pineapple" title="Pineapple">pineapples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potato" title="Sweet potato">sweet potatoes</a> supplemented by <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fish</a> and seafood.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Plaza_Col%C3%B3n_and_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_la_Candelaria_c1898_-_Mayag%C3%BCez_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Plaza_Col%C3%B3n_and_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_la_Candelaria_c1898_-_Mayag%C3%BCez_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Plaza_Col%C3%B3n_and_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_la_Candelaria_c1898_-_Mayag%C3%BCez_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Plaza_Col%C3%B3n_and_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_la_Candelaria_c1898_-_Mayag%C3%BCez_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Plaza_Col%C3%B3n_and_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_la_Candelaria_c1898_-_Mayag%C3%BCez_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Plaza_Col%C3%B3n_and_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_la_Candelaria_c1898_-_Mayag%C3%BCez_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Plaza_Col%C3%B3n_and_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_la_Candelaria_c1898_-_Mayag%C3%BCez_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1441" data-file-height="963" /></a><figcaption>Mayag\xc3\xbcez\'s <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Col%C3%B3n" title="Plaza Col\xc3\xb3n">Plaza Col\xc3\xb3n</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Mayag%C3%BCez" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathedral of Mayag\xc3\xbcez">Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora de la Candelaria church</a> (later cathedral), 1898</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Mayag\xc3\xbcez was founded on September 18, 1760, by a group led by brothers Faustino and Lorenzo Mart\xc3\xadnez de Matos, Juan de Silva and Juan de Aponte, at a hill located about one kilometer inland from <a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez_Bay" title="Mayag\xc3\xbcez Bay">Mayag\xc3\xbcez Bay</a> and the outlet of the <a href="/wiki/Yag%C3%BCez_River" title="Yag\xc3\xbcez River">Yag\xc3\xbcez River</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Crown" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Crown">Spanish Crown</a> granted the founders the right to self-government in 1763, formally separating the town from the larger <i>Partido de <a href="/wiki/San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Germ\xc3\xa1n, Puerto Rico">San Germ\xc3\xa1n</a></i>. The settlement was named <b>Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora de la Candelaria de Mayag\xc3\xbcez</b> (<i>Our Lady of Candelaria of Mayag\xc3\xbcez</i>) to evoke an apparition of the Virgin Mary on the island of <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a>, one of the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>. Most of the town\'s <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islanders" title="Canary Islanders">settlers, including its founders</a>, migrated from the archipelago, whose <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_of_Candelaria" title="Virgin of Candelaria">Virgin of Candelaria</a>.\n</p><p>On May 7, 1836, the settlement was elevated to the royal status of <a href="/wiki/Villa_(chartered_town)" class="mw-redirect" title="Villa (chartered town)">villa</a>, and Rafael Mangual was named its first mayor. At the time, the villa\'s principal economic activity was agriculture. The famous patriot, educator, sociologist, philosopher, essayist and novelist <a href="/wiki/Eugenio_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Hostos" title="Eugenio Mar\xc3\xada de Hostos">Eugenio Mar\xc3\xada de Hostos</a> was born in Mayag\xc3\xbcez in 1839. On July 10, 1877, the villa received its <a href="/wiki/Municipal_corporation" title="Municipal corporation">city charter</a> from the Royal Crown of Spain.\n</p><p>Puerto Rico was ceded by Spain in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War</a> under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_of_1898" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Paris of 1898">Treaty of Paris of 1898</a> and became a territory of the United States.In 1899, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_War" title="United States Department of War">United States Department of War</a> conducted a <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a> of Puerto Rico finding that the population of Mayag\xc3\xbcez was 35,700, making it one of the largest towns in Puerto Rico at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-OfficeSanger1900_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OfficeSanger1900-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The city\'s main Roman Catholic church, <a href="/wiki/Catedral_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_la_Candelaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Catedral Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora de la Candelaria">Our Lady of the Candelaria</a>, was built in a plot consecrated on August 21, 1760. Its first masonry building was erected in 1780. The current church was built in 1836, and was rebuilt in 1922. The redesign by architect Luis Perocier sought to restore the building to its original splendor. The <a href="/wiki/1918_San_Ferm%C3%ADn_earthquake" title="1918 San Ferm\xc3\xadn earthquake">1918 San Ferm\xc3\xadn earthquake</a> had destroyed the temple\'s ceiling, and a lightning bolt struck and tore down a wedge-shaped corner of one of its two bell towers. However, lack of proper funding and the extent of the damage of the original structure forced the rebuilding to be scaled-down considerably.<sup id="cite_ref-Earthquake_1918_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Earthquake_1918-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>\nIn 1911, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Mayag%C3%BCez" title="University of Puerto Rico at Mayag\xc3\xbcez">College of Agriculture and Mechanic Arts</a> was founded in Mayag\xc3\xbcez. Today it is known as the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Mayag%C3%BCez" title="University of Puerto Rico at Mayag\xc3\xbcez">University of Puerto Rico at Mayag\xc3\xbcez</a> (UPRM)\xe2\x80\x94the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>\'s leading engineering institution.</p><figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Structure_in_El_Man%C3%AD,_Sabanetos,_Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico_destroyed_by_Hurricane_Maria.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Structure_in_El_Man%C3%AD%2C_Sabanetos%2C_Mayag%C3%BCez%2C_Puerto_Rico_destroyed_by_Hurricane_Maria.jpg/220px-Structure_in_El_Man%C3%AD%2C_Sabanetos%2C_Mayag%C3%BCez%2C_Puerto_Rico_destroyed_by_Hurricane_Maria.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Structure_in_El_Man%C3%AD%2C_Sabanetos%2C_Mayag%C3%BCez%2C_Puerto_Rico_destroyed_by_Hurricane_Maria.jpg/330px-Structure_in_El_Man%C3%AD%2C_Sabanetos%2C_Mayag%C3%BCez%2C_Puerto_Rico_destroyed_by_Hurricane_Maria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Structure_in_El_Man%C3%AD%2C_Sabanetos%2C_Mayag%C3%BCez%2C_Puerto_Rico_destroyed_by_Hurricane_Maria.jpg/440px-Structure_in_El_Man%C3%AD%2C_Sabanetos%2C_Mayag%C3%BCez%2C_Puerto_Rico_destroyed_by_Hurricane_Maria.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="621" /></a><figcaption>Structure in El Man\xc3\xad, Sabanetos, Mayag\xc3\xbcez destroyed by Hurricane Maria</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Between 1962 and 1998 Mayag\xc3\xbcez was a major <a href="/wiki/Tuna" title="Tuna">tuna</a> canning and processing center. At one time, 80% of all tuna products consumed in the United States were packed in Mayag\xc3\xbcez (the biggest employer, <a href="/wiki/Charlie_the_Tuna" title="Charlie the Tuna">StarKist</a>, had 11,000 employees working three daily shifts in the local plant\'s heyday). Mayag\xc3\xbcez was also a major <a href="/wiki/Textile_industry" title="Textile industry">textile industry</a> hub; almost a quarter of all drill uniforms used by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">United States Army</a> were sewn in the city. Today, Mayag\xc3\xbcez is the fifth-largest city in Puerto Rico and is considered one of the most important cities in the island. The city is centered on the impressive Spanish-style main square <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Col%C3%B3n" title="Plaza Col\xc3\xb3n">Plaza Col\xc3\xb3n</a>, a tribute to <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>, whose statue stands in the middle of the square, surrounded by 16 bronze statues.\n</p><p>Mayag\xc3\xbcez has become a major <a href="/wiki/College_town" title="College town">college town</a> with the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Mayag%C3%BCez" title="University of Puerto Rico at Mayag\xc3\xbcez">UPRM</a>, the now closed <a href="/wiki/Facultad_de_Derecho_Eugenio_Maria_de_Hostos" title="Facultad de Derecho Eugenio Maria de Hostos">Eugenio Mar\xc3\xada de Hostos Law School</a><sup id="cite_ref-Law_School_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law_School-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Catholic_University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Mayag%C3%BCez" title="Pontifical Catholic University of Puerto Rico at Mayag\xc3\xbcez">Pontifical Catholic University of Puerto Rico</a>.\n</p><p>On September 20, 2017 <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> struck Puerto Rico. In Mayag\xc3\xbcez, losses were described as "catastrophic".<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The storm triggered numerous landslides in Mayag\xc3\xbcez. In some areas of Mayag\xc3\xbcez, there were over 25 landslides per square mile due to the deluge.<sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geography">Geography</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Mayag\xc3\xbcez is located near the geographical center of the west coast of Puerto Rico about two to three hours by automobile from <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>. Its land area is 77.6 square miles (201.06&#160;km<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The city\'s terrain includes; coast plains, river valleys, marshland, hills and mountains. Of its multiple rivers and streams, the two most important are the <a href="/wiki/Yag%C3%BCez_River" title="Yag\xc3\xbcez River">R\xc3\xado Yag\xc3\xbcez</a>, which flows from the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Cordillera Central, Puerto Rico">Central Mountain Range</a> through downtown until it empties into the <a href="/wiki/Mona_Passage" title="Mona Passage">Mona Passage</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Guanajibo" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Guanajibo">R\xc3\xado Guanajibo</a>, which flows through several neighborhoods in the southern portion of the municipality until it empties in the <a href="/wiki/Mona_Passage" title="Mona Passage">Mona Passage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="National_protected_areas">National protected areas</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: National protected areas"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Desecheo_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Desecheo National Wildlife Refuge">Desecheo National Wildlife Refuge</a> on <a href="/wiki/Desecheo_Island" title="Desecheo Island">Desecheo Island</a> is a protected area.\n</p><p>To the north of the <a href="/wiki/El_Man%C3%AD" title="El Man\xc3\xad">El Man\xc3\xad</a> community in Mayag\xc3\xbcez is the Boquilla Creek Wildlife Reserve (<i>Reserva Natural del Ca\xc3\xb1o de la Boquilla</i>), a protected area and the habitat of <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">endangered species</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DRNA_map_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DRNA_map-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Climate">Climate</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Climate"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Mayag\xc3\xbcez has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna_climate" title="Tropical savanna climate">tropical savanna climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification</a> <i>Aw</i>). The city has the most extreme weather of the island. The high frequency of severe storms in the summer can produce strong winds, <a href="/wiki/Flood" title="Flood">floods</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waterspout" title="Waterspout">waterspouts</a>, and sometimes <a href="/wiki/Hail" title="Hail">hail</a> and even <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">tornadoes</a>. The average annual temperature is 75&#160;\xc2\xb0F or 23.9&#160;\xc2\xb0C. Winter is usually quite dry and warm, with temperatures between 82&#160;\xc2\xb0F or 27.8&#160;\xc2\xb0C and 55&#160;\xc2\xb0F or 12.8&#160;\xc2\xb0C. Summer is usually very hot and humid, with temperatures reaching 95&#160;\xc2\xb0F or 35&#160;\xc2\xb0C, with heat index of up to 115&#160;\xc2\xb0F or 46.1&#160;\xc2\xb0C. From May to October, most evenings experience strong thunderstorms, due to heat, humidity and the topography of the area.\n</p>\n<div>\n<table class="wikitable mw-collapsible" style="width:auto; Mayag\xc3\xbcez</figcaption></figure>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Barrios">Barrios</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Barrios"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Municipio" title="Municipio">municipio</a></i> has an estimated population of just over 100,000 spread over 21 barrios (<i><a href="/wiki/Barrios_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Barrios of Puerto Rico">barrios</a></i>) including <i>Mayag\xc3\xbcez Pueblo</i> (The downtown area and the administrative center of the city). One of the barrios is <a href="/wiki/Isla_de_Mona_e_Islote_Monito,_Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico" title="Isla de Mona e Islote Monito, Mayag\xc3\xbcez, Puerto Rico">Isla de Mona e Islote Monito</a>, which consists of the offshore islands of <a href="/wiki/Mona,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Mona, Puerto Rico">Mona Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monito_Island" title="Monito Island">Monito Island</a>. This is the largest ward by land area and at the same time the only one without any permanent population. Also, uninhabited <a href="/wiki/Desecheo_Island" title="Desecheo Island">Desecheo Island</a> belongs to the municipality as part of <a href="/wiki/Sabanetas,_Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico" title="Sabanetas, Mayag\xc3\xbcez, Puerto Rico">Sabanetas</a> <i>barrio</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pico_1969_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pico_1969-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law2015_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law2015-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2010_Census_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010_Census-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1184024115">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output Rico">Sabanetas</a></li></ol>\n</div>\n<p><b>Mayag\xc3\xbcez Pueblo</b> is further subdivided into these barrios:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1184024115"><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 20em;">\n<ul><li>Candelaria</li>\n<li>C\xc3\xa1rcel</li>\n<li>Marina Septentrional</li>\n<li>Marina Meridional</li>\n<li>R\xc3\xado</li>\n<li>Salud<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>\n</div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sectors">Sectors</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Sectors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Barrios (which are, in contemporary times, roughly comparable to  <a href="/wiki/Minor_civil_divisions" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor civil divisions">minor civil divisions</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-Barrio-Pueblo_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barrio-Pueblo-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> are further subdivided into smaller areas called <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">sectores</i></span> (<i>sectors</i> in English). The types of <i>sectores</i> may vary, from normally <i>sector</i> to <i>urbanizaci\xc3\xb3n</i> to <i>reparto</i> to <i>barriada</i> to <i>residencial</i>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law_1-2001_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law_1-2001-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The sectors that comprise Mayag\xc3\xbcez City are:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1184024115"><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 20em;">\n<ul><li>Balboa</li>\n<li>Barcelona</li>\n<li>El Seco</li>\n<li>El Liceo</li>\n<li>El Pueblo</li>\n<li>La Mineral</li>\n<li>La Quinta</li>\n<li>Par\xc3\xads</li>\n<li>Trastalleres</li></ul>\n</div>\n<p>Other notable neighborhoods or sectors:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/El_Man%C3%AD" title="El Man\xc3\xad">El Man\xc3\xad</a>\xe2\x80\x94community in Sabanetas</li>\n<li>Mayag\xc3\xbcez Terrace\xe2\x80\x94development in Algarrobo, near the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Mayag%C3%BCez" title="University of Puerto Rico at Mayag\xc3\xbcez">UPRM</a> Campus</li>\n<li>Alturas de Mayag\xc3\xbcez\xe2\x80\x94development in Algarrobo, near the <a href="/wiki/Holiday_Inn" title="Holiday Inn">Holiday Inn Hotel</a> and the Regional Distribution Center</li>\n<li>El Cerro de las Mesas\xe2\x80\x94known for being the home of "<a href="/wiki/Residential_Center_of_Educative_Opportunities_of_Mayag%C3%BCez" title="Residential Center of Educative Opportunities of Mayag\xc3\xbcez">CROEM</a>" and for its picture perfect views of the city from Camino Berrios.</li>\n<li>Buena Vista\xe2\x80\x94a hilltop picturesque community next to the <a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez_barrio-pueblo" title="Mayag\xc3\xbcez barrio-pueblo">downtown area</a>.</li>\n<li>Colombia\xe2\x80\x94a famous former slum, alongside a Government Center.</li>\n<li>Columbus Landing\xe2\x80\x94the second oldest public housing project (<i>caserio</i>) in Puerto Rico.</li>\n<li>Dulces Labios\xe2\x80\x94a picturesque community alongside <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_2" title="Puerto Rico Highway 2">PR-2</a> famous for its history and its musical activities.</li>\n<li>Ensanche Mart\xc3\xadnez (La Bosque)\xe2\x80\x94student area, near the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Mayag%C3%BCez" title="University of Puerto Rico at Mayag\xc3\xbcez">UPRM</a> Campus.</li>\n<li>Ensanche Ram\xc3\xadrez\xe2\x80\x94a hilltop high class development, near the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Mayag%C3%BCez" title="University of Puerto Rico at Mayag\xc3\xbcez">UPRM</a> Campus.</li>\n<li>Ensanche Vivaldi\xe2\x80\x94student area, near the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Mayag%C3%BCez" title="University of Puerto Rico at Mayag\xc3\xbcez">UPRM</a> Campus.</li>\n<li>La Riviera\xe2\x80\x94student area.</li>\n<li>Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n\xe2\x80\x94development in <a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez_Arriba" title="Mayag\xc3\xbcez Arriba">Mayag\xc3\xbcez Arriba</a> next to Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Rivera Park (eastern outskirts).</li>\n<li>Santurce\xe2\x80\x94community next to the Old Municipal Cemetery.</li>\n<li>Vadi-Cristy\xe2\x80\x94community alongside <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_2" title="Puerto Rico Highway 2">PR-2</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez_barrio-pueblo" title="Mayag\xc3\xbcez barrio-pueblo">downtown area</a>.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Special_Communities">Special Communities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Special Communities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Office_for_Socioeconomic_and_Community_Development" title="Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development">Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development</a></div>\n<p><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Comunidades Especiales de Puerto Rico</i></span> (Special Communities of Puerto Rico) are marginalized communities whose citizens are experiencing a certain amount of <a href="/wiki/Social_exclusion" title="Social exclusion">social exclusion</a>. A map shows these communities occur in nearly every municipality of the commonwealth. Of the 742 places that were on the list in 2014, the following barrios, communities, sectors, or neighborhoods were in Mayag\xc3\xbcez: Balboa, Barrio Salud, Buena Vista, Central Igualdad, Dulces Labios, El Man\xc3\xad, El Quemado, Felices D\xc3\xadas, La Chorra, La Quinta, Legu\xc3\xadzamo, Mayag\xc3\xbcez Arriba, Parcelas Rol\xc3\xb3n, Polvor\xc3\xadn, Quebrada Grande, R\xc3\xado Ca\xc3\xb1as, R\xc3\xado Hondo, Rosario, and Trastalleres.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wordpress.com_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wordpress.com-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Demographics">Demographics</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Demographics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236656977">.mw-parser-output .abbr-header{white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output title="2000 United States census"> 2000</a></th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">98,434</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">\xe2\x88\x921.9%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px"><a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_census" title="2010 United States census"> 2010</a></th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">89,080</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">\xe2\x88\x929.5%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px"><a href="/wiki/2020_United_States_census" title="2020 United States census">2020</a></th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">73,077</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">\xe2\x88\x9218.0%</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>According to 2009 U.S. Census Bureau estimates, there were 92,156 people (down from 98,434 in 2000) in 38,469 housing units residing in Mayag\xc3\xbcez. The population density was 1,187 inhabitants per square mile (458/km<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-2009USCENSUS_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009USCENSUS-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2009USCENSUSFACTSheet_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009USCENSUSFACTSheet-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The city has a considerable "college population" adding approximately 10,000 people to the year round population of Mayag\xc3\xbcez. People of <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Hispanic or Latino</a> origin, who may be of any race, composed 98.9% of the population.\n</p><p>Of the 31,877 households in 2007 in Mayag\xc3\xbcez, 38.6% were married couples living together, 22.3% had a female householder with no husband present, and 33.7% were non-families. 33.3% had children under the age of 18 living in them. Of all households 27.8% were made up of individuals, and 9.8% had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.75 and the average family size was 3.41.\n</p><p>In Mayag\xc3\xbcez, the population was spread out, with 26.9% under the age of 18, 10.3% from 18 to 24, 30.8% from 25 to 44, 20.6% from 45 to 64, and 11.5% who were 65 years of age or older. The median age was 33 years. Mayag\xc3\xbcez had more women, with 88.4 males for every 100 females.\n</p><p>As of 2000, speakers of <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> as a first language accounted for 15.14% of the population. <sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable floatleft">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="3">Mayag\xc3\xbcez 2020 census<sup id="cite_ref-Bureau_2021_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bureau_2021-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Race\n</th>\n<th>Population\n</th>\n<th>%\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/White_Puerto_Ricans" title="White Puerto Islander">Pacific Islander</a></td>\n<td>24</td>\n<td>0.0\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Some other race</td>\n<td>16,878</td>\n<td>23.1\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Multiracial_people" title="Multiracial people">Two or more races</a></td>\n<td>38,064</td>\n<td>52.1\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div style="clear:both;" class=""></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The city has had several natural disasters. It faced a major economic downturn due to the closure of its textile factories and tuna industry, which were the principal industries of the city for the greater part of the 20th century. Over 11,000 permanent jobs in these two industries were lost in the city during the 1990s, and because of this, Mayag\xc3\xbcez became the jurisdiction of the United States with the second most industrial job losses during the time, second only to <a href="/wiki/Flint,_Michigan" title="Flint, Michigan">Flint, Michigan</a>. Once the third city in population and importance in Puerto Rico, population numbers for it have been relatively stagnant, and it has lost population.\n</p><p>Mayag\xc3\xbcez has a floating population due to its universities, principally the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Mayag%C3%BCez" title="University of Puerto Rico at Mayag\xc3\xbcez">University of Puerto Rico- Mayag\xc3\xbcez Campus</a> of about 15,000\xe2\x80\x9320,000 which contributes considerably to its economy.\n</p><p>In 2005 Winston-Salem Industries for The Blind was the first industry to move into the city\'s industrial park in many years. In July 2007 <a href="/wiki/Honeywell" title="Honeywell">Honeywell</a> opened a customer support service center for its aerospace and information technology divisions in the city.\n</p><p>As of 2022, <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Labor_Statistics" title="Bureau of Labor Statistics">Bureau of Labor Statistics</a> data revealed that the Mayag\xc3\xbcez metropolitan area had the worst-paid lawyers in the United States, with an annual average salary of only $53,850.<sup id="cite_ref-ABA_Wages_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABA_Wages-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Culture">Culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Contributions_to_Puerto_Rican_gastronomy">Contributions to Puerto Rican gastronomy</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Contributions to Puerto Rican gastronomy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Mayag\xc3\xbcez\'s contributions to <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_cuisine" title="Puerto Rican cuisine">Puerto Rican gastronomy</a> have been many, and a few of these are known outside Puerto Rico. Besides being host to one of the largest concentrations of <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">mango</a> trees in the island, the city has been a host to various food enterprises whose products are popular in Puerto Rico (and  elsewhere):\n</p>\n<ul><li><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es"><a href="/wiki/Brazo_gitano" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazo gitano">Brazo gitano</a></i></span> \xe2\x80\x93 literally "<a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">gypsy</a> arm", is the locally produced <a href="/wiki/Swiss_roll" title="Swiss roll">Swiss or jelly roll</a>, originally from Spain. E. Franco &amp; Co., a bakery, food importer, and restaurant established in the late 1850s, is the best-known provider of <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">brazos gitanos</i></span> in town. Another (more recent) provider is Ricomini Bakery, whose central store in <a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez_barrio-pueblo" title="Mayag\xc3\xbcez barrio-pueblo">downtown Mayag\xc3\xbcez</a> has been open for over 100 years.</li>\n<li>Papalaya \xe2\x80\x93 a <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_cuisine" title="Latin American cuisine">Latin-American cuisine</a> <a href="/wiki/Food_truck" title="Food truck">food truck</a> chain known for its "nachos with <a href="/wiki/Grated_cheese" title="Grated cheese">grated cheese</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pico_de_gallo" title="Pico de gallo">pico de gallo</a></i> and in-house sauce".<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><i>Sangr\xc3\xada de Fido</i> \xe2\x80\x93 the heirs of Wilfrido Aponte still bottle "Sangr\xc3\xada de Fido", a powerful concoction inspired by <a href="/wiki/Sangria" title="Sangria">sangria</a>, but made with fruit juices, <a href="/wiki/Bacardi_151" title="Bacardi 151">Bacardi 151</a> <a href="/wiki/Rum" title="Rum">rum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burgundy_wine" title="Burgundy wine">burgundy wine</a> (technically not from <a href="/wiki/Burgundy_(French_region)" class="mw-redirect" title="Burgundy (French region)">Bourgogne</a>, but produced by <a href="/wiki/E_%26_J_Gallo_Winery" title="E &amp; J Gallo Winery">E &amp; J Gallo Winery</a> in <a href="/wiki/Modesto,_California" title="Modesto, California">Modesto, California</a>). It had been bottled by hand by the bartender since the mid-1970s. <i>"Sangr\xc3\xada de Fido"</i> has a sizeable reputation outside Puerto Rico, and can claim tasters from as far away as California and Spain. <a href="/wiki/E_%26_J_Gallo_Winery" title="E &amp; J Gallo Winery">E &amp; J Gallo</a> once awarded Aponte with a "Customer of the Year" award and flew him to their headquarters. Aponte was reportedly offered $250,000 by <a href="/wiki/Bacardi" title="Bacardi">Bacardi</a> to sell his original recipe once, to which he refused.</li>\n<li>Bolo\'s Sorullitos \xe2\x80\x93 a now-defunct operation that originated at Bolo\'s Restaurant, a seaside eatery next to <a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez_Bay" title="Mayag\xc3\xbcez Bay">Mayag\xc3\xbcez Bay</a>, which produced sorullitos, or fried cornsticks, along with <a href="/wiki/Fry_sauce" title="Fry sauce">mayo-ketchup</a>, a dip made of <a href="/wiki/Mayonnaise" title="Mayonnaise">mayonnaise</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ketchup" title="Ketchup">ketchup</a>, and garlic extract. The restaurant was popular in Puerto Rico between the late 1970s and mid-1980s (its custom-made building now houses <a href="/wiki/WORA-TV" title="WORA-TV">WORA-TV</a>, one of the local television stations). For a while the frozen cornsticks were sold commercially in stores.</li>\n<li>Flan-Es-Ced\xc3\xb3\' \xe2\x80\x93 Elmec Industries, Inc. has been the local <a href="/wiki/Cr%C3%A8me_caramel" title="Cr\xc3\xa8me caramel">flan</a> producer for over thirty years</li>\n<li>India / <a href="/wiki/Cervecer%C3%ADa_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Cervecer\xc3\xada India">Medalla beer</a> \xe2\x80\x93 the only remaining mass-produced <a href="/w/index.php?title=Puerto_Rican_beer&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Puerto Rican beer (page does not exist)">Puerto Rican beer</a> is brewed by "<a href="/wiki/Cervecer%C3%ADa_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Cervecer\xc3\xada India">Cervecer\xc3\xada India</a>", one of the largest employers in town. <i>Mayag\xc3\xbcezanos</i> are queued into morning rush hour, lunch and afternoon rush hour by the company\'s whistle, which rings at 7:00&#160;am, 8:00&#160;am, 12:00&#160;pm, 1:00&#160;p.m. and 5:00&#160;p.m. (all times <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Standard_Time_Zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic Standard Time Zone">AST</a>)</li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rex_Cream%27s_Ice_Cream&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Rex Cream&#39;s Ice Cream (page does not exist)">Rex Cream\'s Ice Cream</a> \xe2\x80\x93 established in the mid-1960s by <a href="/wiki/Chinese_immigration_to_Puerto_Rico" title="Chinese immigration to Puerto Rico">Chinese migrants</a> who came to Puerto Rico by the way of <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a>, Rex Cream is a chain of ice cream parlors that had its heyday in the late 1970s. The two flagship stores in Mayag\xc3\xbcez, however, are still popular (particularly on <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday" title="Good Friday">Good Friday</a>, since one of the stores is the endpoint for a Good Friday religious procession) for producing alternative ice cream flavors, particularly a <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a> <a href="/wiki/Sherbet_(U.S.)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sherbet (U.S.)">sherbet</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tuna" title="Tuna">Tuna fish</a> \xe2\x80\x93 At one time, <a href="/wiki/Charlie_the_Tuna" title="Charlie the Tuna">StarKist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicken_of_the_Sea" title="Chicken of the Sea">Chicken of the Sea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bumble_Bee_(brand)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bumble Bee (brand)">Bumble Bee</a> produced 80% of their collective production for consumption in the United States in Mayag\xc3\xbcez. The last remaining tuna fish cannery closed in 2012 when Bumble Bee shuttered their operation.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>A new distillery was founded in Mayag\xc3\xbcez in 2009, Destiler\xc3\xada Coqu\xc3\xad. Its production is limited to 100 bottles a day, their main product is artisan <a href="/wiki/Rum" title="Rum">rum</a> called <a href="/wiki/Pitorro" title="Pitorro">pitorro</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>A defunct <a href="/wiki/Cola" title="Cola">cola</a> bottling operation in town produced "Vita Cola", a popular soft drink in Puerto Rico between the late 1940s and early 1960s.\n</p><p>Mayag\xc3\xbcez was a major rum producing city in Puerto Rico between the 1930s and 1970s <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. Several brands were produced by the city\'s three rum distillers. The most successful rum producing operation at the time was Jos\xc3\xa9 Gonz\xc3\xa1lez Clemente y Co., the bottlers of Ron Superior Puerto Rico, an award-winning <a href="/wiki/Dark_rum" class="mw-redirect" title="Dark rum">dark rum</a> that was bottled between 1909 and the late-1970s.\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Puerto_Rican_rums" title="List of Puerto Rican rums">List of Puerto Rican rums</a></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Festivals_and_events">Festivals and events</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Festivals and events"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Mayag\xc3\xbcez celebrates its <a href="/wiki/Fiestas_patronales_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Fiestas patronales in Puerto Rico">patron saint</a> festival in late January / early February. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Fiestas Patronales Virgen de la Candelaria</i></span> is a religious and cultural celebration that generally features parades, games, artisans, amusement rides, regional food, and live entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-J.D._2006_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-J.D._2006-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Other festivals and events celebrated in Mayag\xc3\xbcez include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Epiphany_(holiday)" title="Epiphany (holiday)">Three Kings Day</a> Festival \xe2\x80\x93 January</li>\n<li><i>Romance on the Boulevard</i> \xe2\x80\x93 February</li>\n<li>Bomba and plena festival \xe2\x80\x93 February/March</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mother%27s_Day_(United_States)" title="Mother&#39;s Day (United States)">Mothers Day</a> concert \xe2\x80\x93 May</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Father%27s_Day" title="Father&#39;s Day">Fathers Day</a> concert \xe2\x80\x93 June</li>\n<li>Mayag\xc3\xbcez <a href="/wiki/Carnival" title="Carnival">Carnival</a> \xe2\x80\x93 May</li>\n<li>Danza Festival \xe2\x80\x93 May</li>\n<li>Celebration of the founding of Mayag\xc3\xbcez \xe2\x80\x93 September</li>\n<li>Crafts fair \xe2\x80\x93 November</li>\n<li>Christmas festivities \xe2\x80\x93 December</li>\n<li>Anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Flag of Puerto Rico">Puerto Rican flag</a> \xe2\x80\x93 December</li>\n<li>Pedestrian Mayag\xc3\xbcez at <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Col%C3%B3n" title="Plaza Col\xc3\xb3n">Plaza Colon</a> \xe2\x80\x93 third Sunday of the month</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sports">Sports</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Sports"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Natatorium_at_UPRM.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Natatorium_at_UPRM.jpg/220px-Natatorium_at_UPRM.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Natatorium_at_UPRM.jpg/330px-Natatorium_at_UPRM.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Natatorium_at_UPRM.jpg/440px-Natatorium_at_UPRM.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1836" /></a><figcaption>Natatorium built for the 2010 games at the UPR Mayag\xc3\xbcez Campus</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Mayag\xc3\xbcez hosted the <a href="/wiki/2010_Central_American_and_Caribbean_Games" title="2010 Central American and Caribbean Games">2010 Central American and Caribbean Games</a> for which the local and commonwealth governments have provided an investment of $250&#160;million<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> for, among other things, building two new stadiums (the first a re-built <a href="/wiki/Isidoro_Garc%C3%ADa_Baseball_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Isidoro Garc\xc3\xada Baseball Stadium">Isidoro Garc\xc3\xada Baseball Stadium</a> the second next to it a <a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez_Athletics_Stadium" title="Mayag\xc3\xbcez Athletics Stadium">track and field and soccer stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Mayag\xc3\xbcez also hosted the <a href="/wiki/2011_Caribbean_Series" title="2011 Caribbean Series">2011 Caribbean Series</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Mayag\xc3\xbcez\'s National Superior Basketball League (<a href="/wiki/Baloncesto_Superior_Nacional" title="Baloncesto Superior Nacional">BSN</a>) professional basketball team, the <a href="/wiki/Indios_de_Mayag%C3%BCez_(basketball)" title="Indios de Mayag\xc3\xbcez (basketball)">Indios de Mayag\xc3\xbcez</a>, are named in honor of the city\'s Indian heritage. Its baseball winter league team (<a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Baseball_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Baseball League">LBPPR</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Indios_de_Mayag%C3%BCez" title="Indios de Mayag\xc3\xbcez">Indios de Mayag\xc3\xbcez</a>, honor<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> their Indian heritage and the home town\'s <a href="/wiki/Cervecer%C3%ADa_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Cervecer\xc3\xada India">Cervecer\xc3\xada India</a> brewery. The professional soccer club <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Sol" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Sol">Puerto Rico Sol</a>, plays locally at local <i><a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez_Athletics_Stadium" title="Mayag\xc3\xbcez Athletics Stadium">Mayag\xc3\xbcez Athletics Stadium</a></i>.\nThe professional <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a> team <a href="/wiki/Indias_de_Mayag%C3%BCez" title="Indias de Mayag\xc3\xbcez">Indias de Mayag\xc3\xbcez</a> from <a href="/wiki/Liga_de_Voleibol_Superior_Femenino" title="Liga de Voleibol Superior Femenino">Liga de Voleibol Superior Femenino</a>, plays locally at local <i><a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_Recreaci%C3%B3n_y_Deportes" title="Palacio de Recreaci\xc3\xb3n y Deportes">Palacio de Recreaci\xc3\xb3n y Deportes</a></i>.\n</p><p>The "Justas" or inter-university games of the <a href="/wiki/Liga_Atl%C3%A9tica_Interuniversitaria_de_Puerto_Rico" title="Liga Atl\xc3\xa9tica Interuniversitaria de Puerto Rico">Liga Atl\xc3\xa9tica Interuniversitaria de Puerto Rico</a>, were held in Mayag\xc3\xbcez in 2010 in preparation for the <a href="/wiki/2010_Central_American_and_Caribbean_Games" title="2010 Central American and Caribbean Games">Central American and Caribbean Games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\nAlso they were held in 2016 and they are to be held in 2017.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Tourism">Tourism</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Tourism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>There are 13 beaches in Mayag\xc3\xbcez.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Landmarks_and_places_of_interest">Landmarks and places of interest</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: (Second Municipal Theater)</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Gallery">Gallery</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Gallery"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 233.33333333333px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 231.33333333333px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Mayaguez_Customs_House.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Customs House in Marina sector. class="gallerybox" style="width: 175.33333333333px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 173.33333333333px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Nuestrasenoracandelariamayaguez.jpg"
