decoding="async" width="174" height="130" class="mw-file-element" data-file-width="240" data-file-height="180" /></a></span></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">University of Puerto Rico, Mayag\xc3\xbcez \xe2\x80\x93 Portico</div>\n\t\t</li>\n</ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Government">Government</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:MayaguezCityHall.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/MayaguezCityHall.jpg/220px-MayaguezCityHall.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/MayaguezCityHall.jpg/330px-MayaguezCityHall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/MayaguezCityHall.jpg/440px-MayaguezCityHall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a><figcaption>Alcald\xc3\xada de Mayag\xc3\xbcez (Mayag\xc3\xbcez City Hall), 2005</figcaption></figure>\n<p>As one of Puerto Rico\'s 78 <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">municipalities</a>, Mayag\xc3\xbcez\'s government has two executive and legislative branches. Those citizens eligible to vote, directly elect a mayor and the municipal assembly for four-year terms. The municipal government is housed in <a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez_City_Hall" title="Mayag\xc3\xbcez City Hall">Mayag\xc3\xbcez City Hall</a> or <i>Casa Alcaldia</i>, which faces the south side of the Plaza de Colon.\n</p><p>A popularly elected mayor heads the executive branch, currently deputy mayor Jorge Ramos serves in the position as Interim Mayor after the suspension of <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Guillermo_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Guillermo Rodr\xc3\xadguez">Jos\xc3\xa9 Guillermo Rodr\xc3\xadguez</a> from the post pending a investigation. In addition to running the city\'s day-to-day operations and supervising associated departments, the mayor is also responsible for appointing a secretary-auditor and a treasurer.\n</p><p>Mayag\xc3\xbcez\'s Municipal Assembly comprises sixteen elected officials, as defined in the Puerto Rico Law of Autonomous Municipalities of 1991.\n</p><p>The city belongs to the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Puerto_Rico_Senatorial_District_IV&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Puerto Rico Senatorial District IV (page does not exist)">Puerto Rico Senatorial District IV</a>, which is represented by two Senators.\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mayors_of_Mayag%C3%BCez" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayors of Mayag\xc3\xbcez">Mayors of Mayag\xc3\xbcez</a></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Public_services">Public services</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Public services"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Law enforcement in Mayag\xc3\xbcez is the joint responsibility of the Mayag\xc3\xbcez Municipal Police Department and the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Police_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Police Department">Puerto Rico Police Department</a>. The first fire fighters corps in the city was created in 1876.<sup id="cite_ref-HIST_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HIST-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The city has three <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Police" title="Puerto Rico Police">Puerto Rico Police</a> (State Police) facilities and one Municipal Police station, it also has the regional office of the State Emergency Management Bureau(NMEAD) as well as the offices of the Puerto Rico Seismic Network(Red Sismica de Puerto Rico) and the Caribbean Tsunami Warning Program who share facilities in the University of Puerto Rico Mayag\xc3\xbcez Campus.\n</p><p>It has numerous private ambulance service organizations which covered wide parts of the western coast of Puerto Rico and choose Mayag\xc3\xbcez for its central location to the region.\n</p><p>There are small volunteer organizations dedicated to aiding police and emergency services as requested by such.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Symbols">Symbols</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Symbols"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">municipio</i></span> has an official flag and coat of arms.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Flag">Flag</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Flag"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The wide cross represents Christianity brought to the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">New World</a> by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-prfrogui.com_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prfrogui.com-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> who signed his documents with the phrase and the motto <i>Christ Ferens</i>, which means: "He who has Christ." The blue and white waves between the third and fourth quarters recall the coat of arms granted to Columbus by kings <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Monarchs_of_Spain" title="Catholic Monarchs of Spain">Ferdinand and Isabella</a>. The waves represent the ocean (and particularly the <a href="/wiki/Mona_Passage" title="Mona Passage">Mona Passage</a>) through which he sailed to bring the gospel to these new lands. The blue and white waves symbolize the <a href="/wiki/Yag%C3%BCez_River" title="Yag\xc3\xbcez River">Yag\xc3\xbcez River</a> and evokes the nickname <i>City of Pure Waters</i>. The red and white flames on the flag symbolize the traditional <a href="/wiki/Bonfire" title="Bonfire">bonfires</a> of <a href="/wiki/Virgin_of_Candelaria" title="Virgin of Candelaria">Day of Our Lady of Candelaria</a> ("D\xc3\xada de La Candelaria"), ignited in honor of the city\'s <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a> (a tradition started for <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islanders" title="Canary Islanders">Spanish settlers</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-prfrogui.com_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prfrogui.com-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The flag was officially adopted with the signing of City Ordinance 38, signed December 3, 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-prfrogui.com_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prfrogui.com-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Coat of arms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>According to the Puerto Rican historian Federico Ced\xc3\xb3 Alzamora, the original version of the <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a> of Mayag\xc3\xbcez was given to the city December 19, 1894, by the Queen Regent of Spain <a href="/wiki/Maria_Christina_of_Austria" title="Maria Christina of Austria">Maria Christina of Austria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HIST_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HIST-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The upper half of the coat of arms shows the columbine coat of arms recalls and commemorates the discovery of the Island of Borinqu\xc3\xa9n (Puerto Rico) by Columbus in his second trip to the New World in 1493. The lower half of the coat of arms shows a stylized version of Columbus\'s landing on Puerto Rico. The explorer\'s crew disembarked at the western coast of the island,<sup id="cite_ref-HIST_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HIST-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> where several rivers spill their waters in the Mona Passage, among them the Yag\xc3\xbcez, from which the name of Mayag\xc3\xbcez is derived. The present version was reinterpreted by heraldist Roberto Biascochea Lota.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Anthem">Anthem</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Anthem"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The city\'s anthem was written by pianist and former music teacher <a href="/wiki/Luciano_Qui%C3%B1ones" title="Luciano Qui\xc3\xb1ones">Luciano Qui\xc3\xb1ones</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> a long-time resident and now "adopted son" of the city. Until this song\'s adoption, the <a href="/wiki/Plena" title="Plena">plena</a> "<i>A Mayag\xc3\xbcez</i>", written by <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A9sar_Concepci%C3%B3n" title="C\xc3\xa9sar Concepci\xc3\xb3n">C\xc3\xa9sar Concepci\xc3\xb3n</a>, was used by many as an unofficial city song. Qui\xc3\xb1ones\' composition was the winner of a contest sponsored by the city\'s municipality in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-Ced\xc3\xb3_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ced\xc3\xb3-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Mayor Jos\xc3\xa9 Guillermo Rodr\xc3\xadguez and the Municipal Legislature entrusted the Advisory Board of Art and Culture of Mayag\xc3\xbcez to hold a contest to select an anthem for the city.<sup id="cite_ref-Ced\xc3\xb3_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ced\xc3\xb3-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The selected composition was a <a href="/wiki/Danza" title="Danza">danza</a> by Mr Luciano Qui\xc3\xb1ones, who has a bachelor\'s degree in music, a piano professor the Escuela Libre de M\xc3\xbasica de Mayag\xc3\xbcez, he is a music composer already winning nineteen abarrios in competitions held by the Institute of Puerto Rican culture, and the Circulo de Recreo de San Germ\xc3\xa1n.<sup id="cite_ref-Ced\xc3\xb3_58-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ced\xc3\xb3-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The lyrics alludes to the emblematic symbols of Mayag\xc3\xbcez; its nicknames, to its <a href="/wiki/Virgin_of_Candelaria" title="Virgin of Candelaria">Patron Saint</a>, its taste of <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">mango</a>, to its sunsets in the <a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez_Bay" title="Mayag\xc3\xbcez Bay">bay</a>, to the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ta\xc3\xadno people">Ta\xc3\xadno</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Eugenio_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Hostos" title="Eugenio Mar\xc3\xada de Hostos">Eugenio Mar\xc3\xada de Hostos</a>, their role as cultural cradle, the sympathy of the ladies and the dream of its valleys and its mountains.<sup id="cite_ref-Ced\xc3\xb3_58-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ced\xc3\xb3-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The anthem was presented to the people in a memorable concert held in commemoration of the 239 anniversary of the founding of the city on the night of September 18, 1999, interpreted by tenor, Mayag\xc3\xbcez adopted son, Rafael Jos\xc3\xa9 D\xc3\xadaz, Mayag\xc3\xbcezana lyric soprano, Hilda Ramos, accompanied by the Puerto Rico Symphony Orchestra conducted by its Associate Director, Mayag\xc3\xbcezana Roselyn Pab\xc3\xb3n, in the same place where such Symphony Orchestra offered his first concert forty years earlier: the <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Col%C3%B3n" title="Plaza Col\xc3\xb3n">Plaza Col\xc3\xb3n</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ced\xc3\xb3_58-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ced\xc3\xb3-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This danza was recognized as the official anthem of Mayag\xc3\xbcez through the Municipal Ordinance number 58, series 1999\xe2\x80\x932000, adopted on December 20, 1999, by the City Council, which was signed by the Mayor, Honorable Jos\xc3\xa9 Guillermo Rodr\xc3\xadguez on December 24, 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-Ced\xc3\xb3_58-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ced\xc3\xb3-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>MIDI and recorded versions of the anthem can be listened to here.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Education">Education</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Education"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:UPRM_Administration_s.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/UPRM_Administration_s.JPG/220px-UPRM_Administration_s.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/74/UPRM_Administration_s.JPG 1.5x" data-file-width="240" data-file-height="180" /></a><figcaption>UPRM Central Administration Building</figcaption></figure>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Public_schools">Public schools</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Public schools"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Residential_Center_of_Educative_Opportunities_of_Mayag%C3%BCez" title="Residential Center of Educative Opportunities of Mayag\xc3\xbcez">Residential Center for Educative Opportunities of Mayag\xc3\xbcez</a>, (<a href="/wiki/Residential_Center_of_Educative_Opportunities_of_Mayag%C3%BCez" title="Residential Center of Educative Opportunities of Mayag\xc3\xbcez">CROEM</a>) is one of only two public boarding schools in Puerto Rico. The largest public high school in town is Eugenio Mar\xc3\xada de Hostos High School. The other public high school in Mayag\xc3\xbcez is Dr. Pedro Perea Fajardo Vocational High School. The former Jos\xc3\xa9 De Diego High School was finally closed in 2009.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Private_schools">Private schools</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Private schools"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The non-profit <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_Educational_Society" title="Southwestern Educational Society">Southwestern Educational Society</a> (SESO) maintains the Southwestern Community School, an English language college preparatory school. Other private schools include: <a href="/wiki/Colegio_San_Benito" title="Colegio San Benito">Colegio San Benito</a>, (CSB) (<a href="/wiki/Benedict_of_Nursia" title="Benedict of Nursia">Saint Benedict</a> College), the <a href="/wiki/Academia_de_la_Inmaculada_Concepci%C3%B3n" title="Academia de la Inmaculada Concepci\xc3\xb3n">Academia de la Inmaculada Concepci\xc3\xb3n</a> (Academy of the Immaculate Conception), Colegio De La Milagrosa (College of Our Lady of Miracles), the Academia Adventista del Oeste (Western <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Adventist</a> Academy) and Academia Adventista de Bella Vista (Bella Vista Adventist Academy), Theopolis Christian Academy (TCA)\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Colleges_and_universities">Colleges and universities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Mayag\xc3\xbcez has become a major <a href="/wiki/College_town" title="College town">college town</a>, due in part to various higher learning institutions in the city.\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Mayag%C3%BCez" title="University of Puerto Rico at Mayag\xc3\xbcez">University of Puerto Rico at Mayag\xc3\xbcez</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Catholic_University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Mayag%C3%BCez" title="Pontifical Catholic University of Puerto Rico at Mayag\xc3\xbcez">Pontifical Catholic University of Puerto Rico at Mayag\xc3\xbcez</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Antillean_Adventist_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Antillean Adventist University">Antillean Adventist University</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Carlos_Albizu_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Carlos Albizu University">Carlos Albizu University</a></li></ul>\n<p>There are also a number of junior colleges in the city:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Instituto_Comercial_de_Puerto_Rico_Junior_College&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Instituto Comercial de Puerto Rico Junior College (page does not exist)">Instituto Comercial de Puerto Rico Junior College</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Instituto_de_Banca_y_Comercio" title="Instituto de Banca y Comercio">Instituto de Banca y Comercio</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/NUC_University" class="mw-redirect" title="NUC University">NUC University</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Escuela_Hotelera_de_San_Juan_-_Recinto_de_Mayag%C3%BCez&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Escuela Hotelera de San Juan - Recinto de Mayag\xc3\xbcez (page does not exist)">Escuela Hotelera de San Juan - Recinto de Mayag\xc3\xbcez</a></li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Health_care_and_hospitals">Health care and hospitals</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Health care and hospitals"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez_Medical_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mayag\xc3\xbcez Medical Center (page does not exist)">Mayag\xc3\xbcez Medical Center</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hospital_Perea&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hospital Perea (page does not exist)">Hospital Perea</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hospital_San_Antonio&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hospital San Antonio (page does not exist)">Hospital San Antonio</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hospital_Bella_Vista&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hospital Bella Vista (page does not exist)">Hospital Bella Vista</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clinica_Yaguez&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Clinica Yaguez (page does not exist)">Clinica Yaguez</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Policlinica_Bella_Vista&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Policlinica Bella Vista (page does not exist)">Policlinica Bella Vista</a></li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Transportation">Transportation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Transportation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n <figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Trasportando_para_los_(sic)_alturas,_Mayag%C3%BCez.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Trasportando_para_los_%28sic%29_alturas%2C_Mayag%C3%BCez.jpg/250px-Trasportando_para_los_%28sic%29_alturas%2C_Mayag%C3%BCez.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="164" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Trasportando_para_los_%28sic%29_alturas%2C_Mayag%C3%BCez.jpg/375px-Trasportando_para_los_%28sic%29_alturas%2C_Mayag%C3%BCez.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Trasportando_para_los_%28sic%29_alturas%2C_Mayag%C3%BCez.jpg/500px-Trasportando_para_los_%28sic%29_alturas%2C_Mayag%C3%BCez.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1701" data-file-height="1118" /></a><figcaption>Across the mountains, 1908</figcaption></figure>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Roads_and_highways">Roads and highways</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Roads and highways"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The dominant mode of transportation in Puerto Rico is the automobile. Mayag\xc3\xbcez is served by two highways linking it to other parts of the island.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_2" title="Puerto Rico Highway 2">Puerto Rico Highway 2</a> existing as an arterial road is a primary route between <a href="/wiki/Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce</a> to the south-east and <a href="/wiki/Aguadilla,_Puerto_Rico" title="Aguadilla, Puerto Rico">Aguadilla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Arecibo, Puerto Rico">Arecibo</a> to the north and north-east respectively. PR-2 is undergoing a conversion to a freeway between Ponce and Mayag\xc3\xbcez.<sup id="cite_ref-freeway_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freeway-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Another important route in Mayag\xc3\xbcez is <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_102" title="Puerto Rico Highway 102">PR-102</a>. It begins at an intersection with PR-2, about 2 miles north of <a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez_barrio-pueblo" title="Mayag\xc3\xbcez barrio-pueblo">Mayag\xc3\xbcez Pueblo</a> at the Mar y Sol development and runs along Mayag\xc3\xbcez\'s coastal industrial areas to <a href="/wiki/Joyuda" class="mw-redirect" title="Joyuda">Joyuda</a>, where it then turns east and terminates in <a href="/wiki/Sabana_Grande,_Puerto_Rico" title="Sabana Grande, Puerto Rico">Sabana Grande</a>.\n</p><p>The portion of the highway adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/Isidoro_Garc%C3%ADa_Stadium" title="Isidoro Garc\xc3\xada Stadium"><i>Estadio Isidoro Garcia</i></a> was upgraded from a two-lane road into an urban boulevard in anticipation of the <a href="/wiki/2010_Central_American_and_Caribbean_Games" title="2010 Central American and Caribbean Games">2010 Centro-American and Caribbean Games</a> celebrated in Mayag\xc3\xbcez. In addition to this upgrade, an elevated by-pass was constructed from the coastal park site over the <a href="/wiki/Yag%C3%BCez_River" title="Yag\xc3\xbcez River">Yag\xc3\xbcez River</a> ending at the Concordia Housing Project.\n</p><p>There are 41 bridges in Mayag\xc3\xbcez.<sup id="cite_ref-bridge_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bridge-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Public_transportation">Public transportation</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Public transportation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:TranviaMayaguez3.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/TranviaMayaguez3.jpg/220px-TranviaMayaguez3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/TranviaMayaguez3.jpg/330px-TranviaMayaguez3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/TranviaMayaguez3.jpg/440px-TranviaMayaguez3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="520" data-file-height="321" /></a><figcaption>Horse-driven tram, Mayag\xc3\xbcez</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Transportation in Mayag\xc3\xbcez is limited to a trolley service, various private taxi companies and an occasional daytime syndicated <i>p\xc3\xbablico</i> service named Mayag\xc3\xbcez Urbano (Urban Mayag\xc3\xbcez) that provide transportation between the main points of the city at a cost of $2.00 per route. Passenger transportation between Mayag\xc3\xbcez and <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a> is operated by the Linea Sultana, another syndicated service.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The city operates three trolleys, free of charge, which run as shuttles between the downtown area and the <a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_Recreaci%C3%B3n_y_Deportes" title="Palacio de Recreaci\xc3\xb3n y Deportes">Palacio de Recreaci\xc3\xb3n y Deportes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Mayag%C3%BCez" title="University of Puerto Rico at Mayag\xc3\xbcez">University of Puerto Rico at Mayag\xc3\xbcez</a> (UPRM) also runs an internal network of trolleys to carry its students inside campus and between UPRM\'s Mayag\xc3\xbcez Terrace development and Palacio de Recreaci\xc3\xb3n y Deportes,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> linking here with the city\'s trolley service. There are some proposals to expand the municipal trolley service to serve inside the UPRM.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Parada_Escuela_Eugenio_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Hostos.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Parada_Escuela_Eugenio_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Hostos.jpg/220px-Parada_Escuela_Eugenio_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Hostos.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Parada_Escuela_Eugenio_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Hostos.jpg/330px-Parada_Escuela_Eugenio_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Hostos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Parada_Escuela_Eugenio_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Hostos.jpg/440px-Parada_Escuela_Eugenio_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Hostos.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2524" data-file-height="1686" /></a><figcaption>Trolley passing through the university (CAAM)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>For the <a href="/wiki/2010_Central_American_and_Caribbean_Games" title="2010 Central American and Caribbean Games">2010 Central American and Caribbean Games</a> the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Department_of_Transportation_and_Public_Works" title="Puerto Rico Department of Transportation and Public Works">Puerto Rico\'s Department of Transportation and Public Works</a> released an <a href="/wiki/Express_bus_service" class="mw-redirect" title="Express bus service">express public bus system</a> operated with <a href="/wiki/Autoridad_Metropolitana_de_Autobuses" class="mw-redirect" title="Autoridad Metropolitana de Autobuses">Autoridad Metropolitana de Autobuses</a> (San Juan\'s Metropolitan Bus Authority) buses specially assigned to serve the city of Mayag\xc3\xbcez. During the <a href="/wiki/2010_Central_American_and_Caribbean_Games" title="2010 Central American and Caribbean Games">Mayag\xc3\xbcez 2010 Games</a>, this bus network was carrying passengers in a corridor along Highway 2 and some main roads. The UPRM trolleybus network was integrated into this service too. Although suspended after the Mayag\xc3\xbcez 2010 Games ended, the system is expected to be re-established shortly.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Seaport">Seaport</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Seaport"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Mayag%C3%BCez" title="Port of Mayag\xc3\xbcez">Port of Mayag\xc3\xbcez</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mayaguez_port.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Mayaguez_port.jpg/220px-Mayaguez_port.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Mayaguez_port.jpg/330px-Mayaguez_port.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Mayaguez_port.jpg/440px-Mayaguez_port.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1836" /></a><figcaption>View of Mayag\xc3\xbcez port from Ferry terminal to silos pier</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Mayag%C3%BCez" title="Port of Mayag\xc3\xbcez">Port of Mayag\xc3\xbcez</a> is the third busiest port in Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It was base for several years to several tuna and fish companies who made the port a considerable busy one. It was normal to see 3 to 4 ships docked at any given day but due to the Section 936 termination the industries started to leave until 2000 approximately when only the ferry and the <i>Federacion de Industria Agropecuaria</i> silos pier were left. It is located northwest of the central business district along Puerto Rico routes 64, 341, and 3341, and stretches for 3.8 miles (6.1&#160;km) along the coast. Its main canal is 0.4 miles (0.64&#160;km) wide and its depth ranges from 47 to 120 feet (14 to 37&#160;m), the water\'s depth along the piers ranges between 28 and 29 feet (8.5 and 8.8&#160;m). The port is protected from rough seas by reefs which run along its northern and western sections.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On March 16, 2011, a new ferry service to the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> was launched by <a href="/w/index.php?title=America_Cruise_Ferries&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="America Cruise Ferries (page does not exist)">America Cruise Ferries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\nLate 2016 the municipal administration awarded an administration contract to a private company after years of legal disputes and non-complying groups involved. The municipal administration had plans of development for the port back to 2004 when they received a portion of port area from the central government (the ferry pier and terminal) but 12 years later the port has seen little to no progress.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Airport">Airport</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Airport"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Eugenio_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Hostos_Airport" title="Eugenio Mar\xc3\xada de Hostos Airport">Eugenio Mar\xc3\xada de Hostos Airport</a></div>\n<p>Mayag\xc3\xbcez\'s airport, <a href="/wiki/Eugenio_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Hostos_Airport" title="Eugenio Mar\xc3\xada de Hostos Airport">Eugenio Mar\xc3\xada de Hostos Airport</a>, also known as <a href="/wiki/El_Man%C3%AD" title="El Man\xc3\xad">El Man\xc3\xad</a> Airport, has had regular airline services for more than thirty years.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is located 4 miles (6.4&#160;km) north of the central business district in the <a href="/wiki/Sabanetas,_Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico" title="Sabanetas, Mayag\xc3\xbcez, Puerto Rico">Sabanetas</a> barrio. Before being inaugurated in 1955, the airport served as a military base. In the 1970s it had domestic service from <a href="/wiki/Prinair" title="Prinair">Prinair</a>, then from <a href="/wiki/American_Eagle_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="American Eagle Airlines">American Eagle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Air_Lines" title="Eastern Air Lines">Eastern Air Lines</a>\'s regional carrier <i>Eastern Metro Express</i> in the 1980s. After Eastern went bankrupt in 1991, American Eagle remained the only airline serving the airport until it ended service to the city on April 30, 2005, due to poor loads.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For a while, <a href="/wiki/Fina_Air" title="Fina Air">Fina Air</a> served flights to the Dominican Republic before the airline went bankrupt. <a href="/wiki/Cape_Air" title="Cape Air">Cape Air</a> currently serves the airport with five daily flights to <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport" title="Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn International Airport">San Juan</a> during the high season and three daily flights during the low season.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Notable_people">Notable people</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Notable people"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main category: <a href="/wiki/Category:People_from_Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico" title="Category:People from Mayag\xc3\xbcez, Puerto Rico">People from Mayag\xc3\xbcez, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:J._Serrano_official_portrait_(3x4).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/J._Serrano_official_portrait_%283x4%29.jpg/170px-J._Serrano_official_portrait_%283x4%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/J._Serrano_official_portrait_%283x4%29.jpg/255px-J._Serrano_official_portrait_%283x4%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/J._Serrano_official_portrait_%283x4%29.jpg/340px-J._Serrano_official_portrait_%283x4%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="3200" /></a><figcaption>Congressman Jos\xc3\xa9 Serrano</figcaption></figure>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Wilkins_(singer)" title="Wilkins (singer)">Wilkins</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Is a Puerto Rican pop music singer and composer.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Maria_Arrillaga" title="Maria Arrillaga">Maria Arrillaga</a> \xe2\x80\x93 is a Puerto Rican poet who has been a professor at the University of Puerto Rico.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_Luisa_Arcelay" title="Mar\xc3\xada Luisa Arcelay">Mar\xc3\xada Luisa Arcelay</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/J._J._Barea" title="J. J. Barea">J. J. Barea</a> \xe2\x80\x93 former professional basketball player for the <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Mavericks" title="Dallas Mavericks">Dallas Mavericks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Timberwolves" title="Minnesota Timberwolves">Minnesota Timberwolves</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lucy_Boscana" title="Lucy Boscana">Lucy Boscana</a> \xe2\x80\x93 actress and a pioneer in Puerto Rico\'s television industry.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Baudilio_Vega_Berr%C3%ADos" title="Baudilio Vega Berr\xc3\xados">Baudilio Vega Berr\xc3\xados</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Antonio_Duverg%C3%A9" title="Antonio Duverg\xc3\xa9">Antonio Duverg\xc3\xa9</a> \xe2\x80\x93 was a Dominican general of French origin who served in the Dominican War of Independence.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Carlos_Vargas_Ferrer" title="Carlos Vargas Ferrer">Carlos Vargas Ferrer</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eugenio_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Hostos" title="Eugenio Mar\xc3\xada de Hostos">Eugenio Mar\xc3\xada de Hostos</a> \xe2\x80\x93 a Puerto Rican educator, philosopher, intellectual, lawyer, sociologist, novelist, and Puerto Rican independence advocate.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Keylla_Hern%C3%A1ndez" title="Keylla Hern\xc3\xa1ndez">Keylla Hern\xc3\xa1ndez</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gina_Lynn" title="Gina Lynn">Gina Lynn</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Hall of fame Puerto Rican former pornographic actress, model, and stripper.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Alicia_Moreda" title="Alicia Moreda">Alicia Moreda</a> \xe2\x80\x93 a soap opera actress, comedian, and a pioneer in Puerto Rico\'s television industry.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Olga_A._M%C3%A9ndez" title="Olga A. M\xc3\xa9ndez">Olga A. M\xc3\xa9ndez</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Padilla" title="Hern\xc3\xa1n Padilla">Hern\xc3\xa1n Padilla</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Frankie_Ruiz" title="Frankie Ruiz">Frankie Ruiz</a> \xe2\x80\x93 was an American salsa singer and songwriter. He was a major figure in the salsa rom\xc3\xa1ntica era of 80\'s, 90\'s.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Noem%C3%AD_Ruiz" title="Noem\xc3\xad Ruiz">Noem\xc3\xad Ruiz</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Roberto_Roena" title="Roberto Roena">Roberto Roena</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Roberto_Sanchez_Vilella" class="mw-redirect" title="Roberto Sanchez Vilella">Roberto Sanchez Vilella</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_E._Serrano" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 E. Serrano">Jos\xc3\xa9 E. Serrano</a>, U.S. Congressman, 1990 to 2021</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kobbo_Santarrosa" title="Kobbo Santarrosa">Kobbo Santarrosa</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mart%C3%ADn_Travieso" title="Mart\xc3\xadn
